  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_bc268b80-6fdc-4b41-8301-742f290ee5f6'
      });
    }

  <span id="freeText7291124907871025691" style="display:none">Come heck or high water, Gracie Snow is determined to drag the legendary ex-jock Bobby Tom Denton back home to Heaven, Texas, to begin shooting his first motion picture. Despite his dazzling good looks and killer charm, Bobby Tom has reservations about being a movie star — and no plans to cooperate with a prim and bossy Ohio wallflower whom he can’t get off his mind or out of his life. Instead, the hell-raising playboy decides to make her over from plain Jane to Texas wildcat.<br /><br />But nothing’s more dangerous than a wildcat with an angel’s heart in a town too small for a bad boy to hide. And all hell breaks loose when two unforgettable people discover love, laughter, passion — and a match that can only be made in Heaven.</span>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section firstReview">
      

<div id="review_536810450" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/536810450" />
    <a title="Emmie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9413367-emmie"><img alt="Emmie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473523613p2/9413367.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/536810450?book_show_action=true">Feb 15, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Emmie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Emmie" href="/user/show/9413367-emmie">Emmie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer536810450" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6628167446727294226">I've been rereading SEP's books this past month and falling back in love with her novels, as well as catching up on some new ones which I enjoyed immensely.<br/><br/>However, "Heaven, Texas" is NOT one of those books. The romance starts off distastefully with Bobby Tom Denton living the life of a rich, shallow, sexist NFL player who treats women like disposable 'sex' objects. Fine, usually this serves as a starting point for the 'hero' who will display inner worth and grow along the way. Instead, Bobby To</span>
  <span id="freeText6628167446727294226" style="display:none">I've been rereading SEP's books this past month and falling back in love with her novels, as well as catching up on some new ones which I enjoyed immensely.<br /><br />However, "Heaven, Texas" is NOT one of those books. The romance starts off distastefully with Bobby Tom Denton living the life of a rich, shallow, sexist NFL player who treats women like disposable 'sex' objects. Fine, usually this serves as a starting point for the 'hero' who will display inner worth and grow along the way. Instead, Bobby Tom's behavior and attitude not only refuse to improve but instead over the course of the novel plummet into the realm of HORRIFYING.<br /><br />As Gracie's trying to leave Bobby Tom and restore her means of self-respect, Bobby Tom breaks out of jail after a night spent assaulting his friends and being a mean drunk "sonovabitch", chases her down in a stolen squad car, and as she's running from him in terror -- a tiny 5'4'' woman against a tall, heavily muscled professional football player -- he's yelling at her to stop and ends up tackling her on the side of the road. Following this, as he's physically dominating her, she's begging him and crying for him to "Stop!" only to be rescued by the cops who arrest Bobby Tom.<br /><br />Upon seeing Bobby Tom resisting arrest, which results in his getting roughly handled by the arresting officer, Gracie leaps on the cop's back and starts screaming that he let Bobby Tom go free.<br /><br />This isn't a romance. It's a codependent horror story about a spoiled selfish man's devolving into an abusive, misogynist asshole and the woman who loves him despite how horribly he treats her and who cannot escape him. The reason Gracie called off their engagement in the first place was because he'd brutally rebuffed her efforts to help him and then he'd tried to force her to have sex with him, dominating her as she's once again yelling at him, "Stop!" and beating him until her hands are hurting. He apologizes, of course, never meaning for her to have hurt herself trying to get him to stop abusing her -- only for this behavior to be repeated in the climactic final scene without any sign of Bobby Tom or any aspect of the novel acknowledging this repetition establishes a pattern of abuse. There's no resolution, simply Gracie loving Bobby Tom despite his terrorizing her as he finally proclaims his love. And somehow this is supposed to be a happy ending?<br /><br />The ending is absolutely appalling as the Mayor and Bobby Tom's family arrive on the highway and the cop, who was in the process of arresting fugitive Bobby Tom, is castigated for upholding the law. Bobby Tom is released, he gets a few sharp words about getting into drunken brawl with a childhood friend, but any efforts to hold him to account for his horrifyingly abusive behavior is dismissed as everyone starts joking about how Gracie can't marry Bobby Tom until she passes the Football Test. What follows is Bobby Tom dumbing down the questions so Gracie is ~worthy~ of marrying this abusive piece of shit who just so happens to have won two Superbowls and is Heaven, Texas' favorite son.<br /><br />This novel is a throwback to the 'rape is romantic' tropes of the 70s and 80s. And I'm happy to say that SEP revisits this formula of handsome blonde charming Stars quarterback and spunky unattractively dressed woman with great personality in "Natural Born Charmer" -- only SEP finally gets it right with Dean Robillard and Blue Bailey. <br /><br />I'm deleting this book from my Kindle and I wish I could burn it from my memory. I've never been so disappointed by the ending of a romance novel before, as I watched what essentially amounted to a woman fleeing her ex in terror suddenly turn into her getting sucked back into his dysfunction and defending him from the only goddamn person in town who was holding him accountable for being a abusive asshole who's breaking laws right and left. The painful irony is that earlier in the novel, Bobby Tom becomes outraged at the suggestion that his mother's lover "raped" her. <br /><br />This book was in desperate need of a deus ex machina to swoop down from on high and rescue Gracie from Bobby Tom. Usually, at the end of these novels, there's this pleasant feeling as you close the book and you imagine the couple's happy future. Instead, I'm imagining how Bobby Tom's struggles to find meaning and direction in his life after having to quit the NFL due to an injury -- well, that'll no doubt be taken out on Gracie. <br /><br />Instead of watching a rough hero reform, this novel gives us a sexist guy who initially appears charming and misunderstood on the surface and shows his horrifying descent into abusing a woman who loves him, who actually has enough self-respect to try to leave her abuser, only for him to chase her down and tackle her and refuse to let her leave him.<br /><br />This is a horror story that attempts to romanticize the "hero"s misogyny and violence against the heroine. Gracie's terror in the final scene and how it suddenly evaporates into sympathy for her abuser's pain, leading to their getting back together and getting married -- it makes me shudder at how it glorifies the sexism and violence.<br /><br />I realize I'm rambling and repeating myself at this point. This isn't a cool and collected review. I'm genuinely horrified by how Bobby Tom's descent into villainy is brushed aside by everyone in town and by Gracie herself -- that final scene between Bobby Tom and Gracie is what I'd expect from a villain in a romance novel right before the hero swoops in and beats the shit out of him, rescuing the heroine, professing his love, they all live happily ever after, yadda yadda yadda. <br /><br />Yet there is no one to stop Bobby Tom, not even the police can stop this superstar football God born and raised in Heaven, Texas. More like Hell, Texas. Poor Gracie. There's no escaping Hell no matter how fast she runs. </span>
  <a data-text-id="6628167446727294226" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1204740535" />
    <a title="Karen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6972914-karen"><img alt="Karen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529600203p2/6972914.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1204740535?book_show_action=true">Feb 18, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Karen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Karen" href="/user/show/6972914-karen">Karen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6972914-karen?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1204740535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11842949115470551186"><b>5 STARS</b><br/><span>[image error]</span><a href='http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men2/cowboy12.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009123._SX540_.jpg' alt=' photo cowboy12.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>What a shocker! I have no idea how she did it, but Susan Elizabeth Phillips managed the impossible. I went into this one with a bad attitude. Yes.. I had absolutely no interest in a character named Bobby Tom anything. And even the heroine left me feeling completely B O R E D...*yawn* But somehow I ended up absolutely LOVING this book!!!<br/><br/><b>
  <i>“There’s no accounting for the mysteries of the human heart” </i>
</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><a href='http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men2/d1ca3397197a53d21df3b464cc39521d.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009124._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo d1ca3397197a53d21df3b464cc39521d.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>Bobby Tom Denton</b> was in the height of his career as the </span>
  <span id="freeText11842949115470551186" style="display:none"><b>5 STARS</b><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men2/cowboy12.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009123._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo cowboy12.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>What a shocker! I have no idea how she did it, but Susan Elizabeth Phillips managed the impossible. I went into this one with a bad attitude. Yes.. I had absolutely no interest in a character named Bobby Tom anything. And even the heroine left me feeling completely B O R E D...*yawn* But somehow I ended up absolutely LOVING this book!!!<br><br><b>
  <i>“There’s no accounting for the mysteries of the human heart” </i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men2/d1ca3397197a53d21df3b464cc39521d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009124._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo d1ca3397197a53d21df3b464cc39521d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>Bobby Tom Denton</b> was in the height of his career as the all-star wide receiver for the Chicago Stars football team. When a bad hit blew out his knee and ended his career at the age of 33, he was at a loss with what to do with the rest of his life. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/e9d4389080044b05e16d72452d1663ef.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009125._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo e9d4389080044b05e16d72452d1663ef.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>After two Super Bowl wins behind him, he had all the money he could ever want, and gorgeous women were lining up in droves to take the quiz… to be Mrs. Bobby Tom Denton. Even his hometown of Telarosa, Texas was pulling out all the stops to make him a living legend. So why was he feeling so lost?<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/superbowl2_1.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009126.jpg" alt=" photo superbowl2_1.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>With nothing better to do, Bobby Tom signed a movie deal. But when the time came to get it started, he couldn’t find the guts to return to his hometown for the filming. So he decided to just ignore it. He'd get there eventually... when he was ready. Maybe.<br><br><b>
  <i>“I happen to be immature, undisciplined, and self-centered, pretty much a little boy in a man's body, although I'd appreciate it if you didn't quote me on that.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Women%202/b3b0c328130eb7686fe7393cc0b36cbe.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009127._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo b3b0c328130eb7686fe7393cc0b36cbe.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Enter <b>Gracie Snow</b>. A thirty year old virgin from Nowhere, Ohio, who grew up practically living in the nursing home her parents worked for. Now working as a production assistant for the up and coming movie company, Gracie’s make-it-or-break-it moment rides on her successfully delivering Bobby Tom to movie set, ASAP. So, in her rumply, oversized navy, J C Penny suit, Gracie shows up at Bobby Tom’s Chicago home to escort him back to Telarosa, Texas. <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/7171610147863aa77ccf453884d20655.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426383994i/14009387._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 7171610147863aa77ccf453884d20655.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>But of course, he isn’t the least bit interested in going with her. He’s got a big party going on… and oh, did I mention that the stripper is late…<br><br><b>
  <i>”Stella said you were hot, but I told her I wanted a blonde.” He regarded her doubtfully. “Bobby Tom likes blondes. Are you blonde under that wig?”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Animated%20gifs/51A738CA-3D75-4541-919F-AB5B991FF174.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1415915107ra/11864653.gif" alt=" photo 51A738CA-3D75-4541-919F-AB5B991FF174.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>”Has it occurred to anybody at Windmill Studios that sending you after me was pretty much like sending a lamb to the slaughter?”</i>
</b><br><br>So, honestly… I started out thinking… what desirable qualities does this Bobby Tom even have? What’s with the hero worship? He’s a redneck peacock for God-sakes! And Gracie was about the equivalent to a worn-out doormat with stars in her eyes. And he wanted nothing to do with her. So how in the hell did these two get together? <br><br><b>
  <i>He was Bobby Tom Denton, for chrissake. He might be retired, but that didn’t mean he’d sunk so low he had to get it on with a charity case like Gracie Snow.</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/210bcb1cb33ba4d253007fe0ada5e43e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009128.jpg" alt=" photo 210bcb1cb33ba4d253007fe0ada5e43e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>All I can say is… a little maybelline, a new hair cut, a tight pair of blue jeans and a lot of spunk is all the magic she needed. She'd already gotten under his skin, and a little <i>ice cream</i> on that cake pretty much sealed the deal. <br><br>It was such a cute, romantic and hilariously funny story of unlikely love!!! And it kept me glued to the pages until the bitter end! And I loved every stinkin’ second of it!!! <br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Women%202/d7c91b2659522f73e62a2943499fcd45.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009129._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo d7c91b2659522f73e62a2943499fcd45.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>”Gracie Snow, you’re turning into a trashy woman right before my eyes.”</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Couples/91cd04f6cb407267b02546695e537da8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009130.jpg" alt=" photo 91cd04f6cb407267b02546695e537da8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>“He settled his hat back into position. She was a rookie in her first big game, and he’d never let her see how close she’d come to unseating a champion” </i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Men2/765a5e61cdbb787745856d46c36c11aa.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009131._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 765a5e61cdbb787745856d46c36c11aa.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>”Those women don’t know how lucky they are,” she muttered. <br>“What women are you talking about?”<br>“All of them who were fortunate enough to fail your football quiz.” He chuckled, lit up a cigar.</i>
</b> <br><br>I won’t say too much more. It’s better discovered as it all unfolds!. And the ending was just epic! A real "Hollywood” moment... a stolen police car, a highway chase, and an earth shattering revelation!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/ford-thunderbird-57-front-david-dunham.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009132._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo ford-thunderbird-57-front-david-dunham.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>
  <i>He’d been playing hide and seek with the truth too long, and he knew the moment of reckoning had finally come. If he wanted to keep facing himself in the mirror every morning, he had to set aside his misgivings about mercy fucking and do what needed to be done.</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Tags/115b615ad99f7a2254acfe3714fe78d8.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009133.jpg" alt=" photo 115b615ad99f7a2254acfe3714fe78d8.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I love this writer. I don’t know how she does it… but she just does. ;) Now, go read this book!<br><br><span>[image error]</span><a href="http://s1253.photobucket.com/user/kgourgues/media/Objects%203/3aa91a8aa07a4d13453d3e80daa2db5c.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1426382328i/14009134._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 3aa91a8aa07a4d13453d3e80daa2db5c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_52716298" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/52716298" />
    <a title="Shawna" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna"><img alt="Shawna" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1574172018p2/1802746.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/52716298?book_show_action=true">Apr 14, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shawna" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shawna" href="/user/show/1802746-shawna">Shawna</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>


          <div><span class="uitext greyText">Recommends it for: </span>
           <span class="uitext reviewText">Fans of funny, sexy contemporary romance, plain jane wallflower heroines, &amp; hot ex-jock playboys</span></div>

        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=heroine-prim-proper-decorous">heroine-prim-proper-decorous</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-asshat-award-hall-of-shame">hero-asshat-award-hall-of-shame</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-i-disliked-much-of-the-book">hero-i-disliked-much-of-the-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=cowboy-stud-fever">cowboy-stud-fever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=heroine-ridiculed-unpopular-teased">heroine-ridiculed-unpopular-teased</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=series-chicago-stars">series-chicago-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-bad-boy-playboy-player">hero-bad-boy-playboy-player</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-not-enough-groveling">hero-not-enough-groveling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1802746-shawna?shelf=hero-stud-mantel-hall-of-fame">hero-stud-mantel-hall-of-fame</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer52716298" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18029624105600152159">4-4 ½ stars – Contemporary Romance <br/><br/>I liked SEP’s witty writing, laugh-out-loud humor, and steamy love scenes, but the hero’s crappy treatment of the heroine made me spitting nails mad at times. I just kept thinking, “why does she put up with his sh*t”?!?! <br/><br/>Retired football legend Bobby Tom Denton might be a sexy as sin, insatiably flirtatious, happy-go-lucky, infectiously funny, womanizing, hellraising, aw shucks ma’am cowboy with killer bedroom skills and a sh*t-eating grin, but he’s also an ego</span>
  <span id="freeText18029624105600152159" style="display:none">4-4 ½ stars – Contemporary Romance <br /><br />I liked SEP’s witty writing, laugh-out-loud humor, and steamy love scenes, but the hero’s crappy treatment of the heroine made me spitting nails mad at times. I just kept thinking, “why does she put up with his sh*t”?!?! <br /><br />Retired football legend Bobby Tom Denton might be a sexy as sin, insatiably flirtatious, happy-go-lucky, infectiously funny, womanizing, hellraising, aw shucks ma’am cowboy with killer bedroom skills and a sh*t-eating grin, but he’s also an egotistical, immature, cocky, and sometimes mean jerk who treats Gracie like a pity friend, mercy f*ck who should be kissing his royal purple cowboy boots, for almost the entire book. Gracie Snow is a prim, quirky, sexually frustrated, 30-year-old virgin, Ohio wallflower who’s insecure about her supposedly Plain Jane looks, but she’s also funny, smart, strong-willed, giving, sweet, feisty, selfless, loving, spirited, and kind. And she deserves a whole lot more than someone who acts like they’re doing some huge, inconvenient cosmic favor by just spending time with her. I actually found myself thinking that Gracie might be better off just driving into the sunset, without Mr. Bobby Tom Denton, and I was a little disappointed with the ending because I wanted about two more chapters and an epilogue of some serious groveling on his part. <br /><br />I really liked the secondary romance between Bobby Tom’s widowed mom Suzy and the former local bad boy turned wealthy, powerful corporate executive, Wayland Sawyer. In fact, I thought their intriguing relationship almost stole the spotlight from main couple, Bobby and Gracie.<br /><br />Overall, I really enjoyed this fun, sexy contemporary romance, but I would have liked it even more and given it full 5 stars had the playboy charmer been taken down a peg or ten and done a little added soul searching and a whole lot more begging!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="18029624105600152159" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Christina ~ Brunette Reader by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/3820197-jill">Jill</a>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=kindle">kindle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/19958389-christina-brunette-reader?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1522013362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8752832122386807794"><br/>After having read and really liked a couple of the more recent books in the Chicago series, I backpedalled to this vintage title (1995) and was just as much pleasantly surprised. What I've come to recognise as SEP's trademarks by now were all already there, from the engaging and smooth prose to the scrumptious dialogues, taking romantic comedy and, in this case, the "opposites attract" trope to a higher level.<br/>Yes, she needed to become a little less accommodating and yes, he often tended to be a </span>
  <span id="freeText8752832122386807794" style="display:none"><br />After having read and really liked a couple of the more recent books in the Chicago series, I backpedalled to this vintage title (1995) and was just as much pleasantly surprised. What I've come to recognise as SEP's trademarks by now were all already there, from the engaging and smooth prose to the scrumptious dialogues, taking romantic comedy and, in this case, the "opposites attract" trope to a higher level.<br />Yes, she needed to become a little less accommodating and yes, he often tended to be a little too smug for his own good, but plain Gracie Snow and NFL golden boy Bobby Tom's love story was so deliciously fun, sexy and sweet and the perfectly ticking sense of humour brought the small town cast and all its antics to life so vividly as to make this book an older gem that hasn't age a day, to savour from start to finish.<br /><br />Buddy-read with Jill :) <br /></span>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1297626328" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1297626328" />
    <a title="Angela (Reading Frenzy Book Blog)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/38657470-angela-reading-frenzy-book-blog"><img alt="Angela (Reading Frenzy Book Blog)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1420222674p2/38657470.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1297626328?book_show_action=true">Jun 03, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Angela (Reading Frenzy Book Blog)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Angela (Reading Frenzy Book Blog)" href="/user/show/38657470-angela-reading-frenzy-book-blog">Angela (Reading Frenzy Book Blog)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38657470-angela-reading-frenzy-book-blog?shelf=4-stars">4-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38657470-angela-reading-frenzy-book-blog?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38657470-angela-reading-frenzy-book-blog?shelf=jock-straps-r-us">jock-straps-r-us</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38657470-angela-reading-frenzy-book-blog?shelf=library-loan">library-loan</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1297626328" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3873804421354639719">Susan Elizabeth Phillips has a unique way of combining romance with laugh out loud humor and then mixing in unusual characters to create an engaging rom com story. Heaven, Texas has her distinctive funny, sexy style written all over it. This is the second book in the Chicago Stars series but can be read as a standalone. While I didn’t like this book as much as <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73070.It_Had_to_Be_You__Chicago_Stars___1_' title='It Had to Be You (Chicago Stars, #1) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips' rel='nofollow noopener'>It Had to Be You</a>, I still found it to be quite enjoyable.<br/><br/>The story surrounds Bobby Tom Denton, a good ole southern boy. He’s a ladies man</span>
  <span id="freeText3873804421354639719" style="display:none">Susan Elizabeth Phillips has a unique way of combining romance with laugh out loud humor and then mixing in unusual characters to create an engaging rom com story. Heaven, Texas has her distinctive funny, sexy style written all over it. This is the second book in the Chicago Stars series but can be read as a standalone. While I didn’t like this book as much as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73070.It_Had_to_Be_You__Chicago_Stars___1_" title="It Had to Be You (Chicago Stars, #1) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">It Had to Be You</a>, I still found it to be quite enjoyable.<br><br>The story surrounds Bobby Tom Denton, a good ole southern boy. He’s a ladies man who prefers leggy blondes with huge boobs and lots of makeup. Bobby Tom is sexy, irresistibly charming, generous to a fault, affable, but very stubborn.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I happen to be immature, undisciplined, and self-centered, pretty much a little boy in a man's body, although I'd appreciate it if you didn't quote me on that.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436073287i/15415874._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo BobbyTom1_zpswsyynx6c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>He’s a 33 year-old two-time Super Bowl champion who is struggling with an identity crisis after a career-ending injury. Bobby Tom is due to begin filming his first movie in his small hometown in Texas. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436073397i/15415892.jpg" alt=" photo football2_zpshpu68y5c.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gracie Snow is a production assistant for the film and she has been tasked with escorting Bobby Tom from Chicago to the movie set on time. At 30 years old she never thought she’d still be a virgin. Gracie is a Plain Jane and one huge walking fashion disaster – from her bad haircut to her ill-fitted matronly clothes. Gracie has led a sheltered life. She’s sweet, altruistic, curious, witty, giving, and very bossy.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436073450i/15415895.jpg" alt=" photo FashionDont1b_zpsdik9wkak.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gracie and Bobby Tom get off to a rocky start but they get to know each other better when they set off on a road trip to Heaven, TX. They finally arrive at his hometown where he receives a hero’s welcome. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“The cowboys named it Heaven because it had the best whorehouses between San Antone and Austin.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436073503i/15415896.jpg" alt=" photo Heaven1_zpsptz2c5fj.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>It becomes clear that everyone wants something from Bobby Tom: money, an autograph, time, a favor, sex. The town seems to be filled with selfish people who think he owes them for his success. It irritated me the way Bobby Tom let everyone walk all over him. Women are lined up around the block day and night to get some of that Bobby Tom lovin’ so in an effort to fend off their advances he and Gracie concoct a story about them being engaged. Since nobody would believe he could fall for someone as homely as Gracie he arranges for her to have a complete makeover. Although the lines between fantasy and reality are in danger of being crossed, Gracie enters the scheme with open eyes and a vow to take nothing from Bobby Tom.<br><blockquote>
  <b>Her sense of honor wouldn’t allow her to take anything from him the way everybody else did. She would give herself to him out of the fullness of her heart, not with the hope of receiving anything in return. And when it was over, this man who had been kissed by the gods would at least be able to remember that Gracie Snow was the one person in his life who had never taken anything from him.</b>
</blockquote><br>I love how independent and feisty Gracie is. She puts Bobby Tom in his place when nobody else will. Even though she’s led a sheltered life, she’s not afraid to try new things. She’s willing to risk her heart for momentary happiness and wonderful memories. She often refers to herself as homely and acknowledges her fashion faux pas but I never thought of her as being ugly. Her humor, her selflessness, and her many acts of kindness make her appealing. The makeover merely brings out the pretty girl who was always lurking there but who was never taught how to flourish.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436074770i/15416078._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo Gracie1_zpszlerywyz.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Bobby Tom and Gracie make a fun pair and I love their verbal sparring as well as their easy joking. There are a couple moments that manage to be simultaneously hilarious and sexy. I’ll never look at Neapolitan ice cream the same way again. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Sweetheart, I don’t think there’s going to be any pain, if that’s what you’re worried about. Now I’m no gynecologist, but you’re thirty years old, and whatever barrier might have been there when you were a youngster has got to have evaporated from old age by now.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1436074770i/15416079._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo couple1_zpso3c56duu.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>However, I wish there was more sexual tension between the two. Maybe it’s the repeated reminders that Gracie doesn’t look like Bobby Tom’s type (she doesn’t have big breasts and she’s not gorgeous) but they seem more like friends with benefits than real lovers. Bobby Tom likes her but he never tries to make her feel desirable. He likes having sex with her but it seems more about scratching an itch than feeling attracted to her. In fact, he tells himself that she’s a charity case but acknowledges he enjoys her company more than anyone else. It makes him seem shallow in my eyes for most of the book and I wanted to shake Gracie for selling herself short.<br><br>There’s an interesting little side plot involving the economic stability of the town and Bobby Tom’s mother who is a grieving widow. Many zany characters are introduced as old relationships are tested and new friendships are forged.<br><br>The unforgettable all-hell-breaks-loose ending is not to be missed! It alone is makes the book worth reading. The story concludes without an epilogue, however, leaving an air of uncertainty. What are Bobby Tom’s plans for the future? Will he continue acting or go into philanthropic work? What will Gracie’s role be? Where will they live? Has Bobby Tom come to terms with prematurely ending his football career? <b>Luckily Susan Elizabeth Phillips has now posted an <a href="http://susanelizabethphillips.com/epilogue-to-heaven-tx/" rel="nofollow noopener">Epilogue</a> on her website!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="3873804421354639719" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_298046481" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/298046481" />
    <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe"><img alt="Natalie Monroe" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1339730817p2/6688207.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/298046481?book_show_action=true">Mar 20, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Natalie Monroe" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Natalie Monroe" href="/user/show/6688207-natalie-monroe">Natalie Monroe</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june">pants-are-snowmen-and-they-are-june</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=guilty-pleasures">guilty-pleasures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/6688207-natalie-monroe?shelf=fabulous-five-stars">fabulous-five-stars</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer298046481" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1775363870460039246"><i>
  <blockquote>“You have an unusual house. Have you lived here long?"<br/><br/>"A couple of years. I don't much like it myself, but the architect is real proud of it. She calls it urban Stone Age with a Japanese Tahitian influence. I sort of just call it ugly.” </blockquote>
</i><br/><br/>Imma let you in on a little secret. <br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425995620ra/13959290.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>This is the novel I read after <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_' title='Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James' rel='nofollow noopener'>Fifty Shades of Grey</a> to purge myself of that monstrosity of a romance/erotica. In many aspects, their plots are similar: virgin, old-fashioned heroines; billionaire, good-looking male leads an</span>
  <span id="freeText1775363870460039246" style="display:none"><i>
  <blockquote>“You have an unusual house. Have you lived here long?"<br><br>"A couple of years. I don't much like it myself, but the architect is real proud of it. She calls it urban Stone Age with a Japanese Tahitian influence. I sort of just call it ugly.” </blockquote>
</i><br><br>Imma let you in on a little secret. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425995620ra/13959290.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This is the novel I read after <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/10818853.Fifty_Shades_of_Grey__Fifty_Shades___1_" title="Fifty Shades of Grey (Fifty Shades, #1) by E.L. James" rel="nofollow noopener">Fifty Shades of Grey</a> to purge myself of that monstrosity of a romance/erotica. In many aspects, their plots are similar: virgin, old-fashioned heroines; billionaire, good-looking male leads and non-committal sex (at least at first). <br><br>But like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/12578077.Obsidian__Lux___1_" title="Obsidian (Lux, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">Obsidian</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/41865.Twilight__Twilight___1_" title="Twilight (Twilight, #1) by Stephenie Meyer" rel="nofollow noopener">Twilight</a>, one of these things is better than the other and it sure as hell ain't the one that tries to pass off <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/32261.Tess_of_the_D_Urbervilles" title="Tess of the D'Urbervilles by Thomas Hardy" rel="nofollow noopener">Tess of the D'Urbervilles</a> as an analogy for their epic love story.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425995620ra/13959291.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So without further ado, <b>why Heaven, Texas deserves to be better-known than Fifty Shades of Gray.<br><br>Reason #1: Gracie is homely and doesn't give a fuck</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"She was of medium height, neither shirt enough to be cute, nor tall enough to be willowy. Although she was flat chested, she was the next closet thing. Her eyes were neither a warm brown nor a sparkling blue, but a nondescript gray. Her mouth was too wide, her chin too stubborn... She concentrated on being grateful for the more important gifts God had given her: intelligence, a quirky sense of humor, and an insatiable interest in all aspects of the human condition."<br>
</blockquote>
</i><br><br>Gracie has other shit to focus on. She runs a nursing home and concentrates on doing her damn job as a production assistant. Although she thinks herself unworthy of Bobby Tom's attention initially, she changes and finds self-worth on her own terms. <br><br>It's okay to be insecure. It's not okay to be so self-deprecating that you talk down every single one of your qualities until a man comes along to restore your self-worth. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425995620ra/13959292.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Reason #2: She's not a blind doormat.</b><br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"This fierce love she felt for him wouldn't keep her from seeing him clearly, the good and the bad, his monstrous ego and too soft heart, his keen intelligence and deadly manipulative charm. Her love wouldn't let her compromise her principles either."</blockquote>
</i><br><br>She fights Bobby Tom over and over, from hauling his ass to the movie set at the start to refusing his money because she doesn't want to take anything from him. Everyone takes something from Bobby Tom, be it a loan or a promise to show up at someone's birthday party. She can't give him anything that he doesn't already have, so she's settling for taking nothing.<br><br><b>Reason #3: Bobby Tom is not an abusive asshat.</b><br><br>This is a very important reason.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425995620ra/13959293.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Gracie gets drunk at one point and throws herself at him, lacy lingerie and all. Bobby Tom, yet un-reformed womanizing ass, coaxes her back into her clothes. Later, when she's sober, they work out out an agreement allowing them to bang their brains out <i>consensually.</i><br><br>The one and only time he attempts to shut Gracie up with his dick, this happens:<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>"Her hands were throbbing with pain. She took one last swing at him and settled back on her heels. Her chest heaved as she clutched her blouse closed. His physical aggression hadn't been about sex, it had been about power, and at the moment she hated him for it. <br><br>[...]<br><br>He pressed something cold between her hands, ice cubes wrapped in a dishtowel. ... "I never did anything like that to a woman in my life. Gracie, I'm sorry. I'd do anything in the world to take back what happened."</blockquote>
</i><br><br>He fucking <i>apologizes</i>. It'd been a dick move and he knows. Christian Gray would rather hang himself with his steel-gray tie than admit he did something. On account of how he likes to be in control and all. His go-to move is shutting Ana up with sex.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425740219ra/13926037.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Skip Fifty Shades and read Heaven, Texas. All the gooey, fuzzy sensation of devouring a romance with none of the rape-culture crap. <br><br>Am I right, Ellen?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1425995620ra/13959294.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="1775363870460039246" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_719495741" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/719495741" />
    <a title="Ingie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/15589375-ingie"><img alt="Ingie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1477339772p2/15589375.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/719495741?book_show_action=true">Sep 14, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ingie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ingie" href="/user/show/15589375-ingie">Ingie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Ingie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=books-i-read-2014">books-i-read-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=c-amazing-5-stars-2014">c-amazing-5-stars-2014</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/15589375-ingie?shelf=romance-m-f-contemporary">romance-m-f-contemporary</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer719495741" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17949397978135078509"><i>Written January 26, 2014</i><br/><br/><b>5 Huge Stars - stunning romantic and hilarouis fun -<br/>I loved every single page - a true joy to read - simply amazing good!!</b><br/><br/>Our dear hero Bobby Tom Denton:<br/><blockquote>“I happen to be immature, undisciplined, and self-centered, pretty much a little boy in a man's body, although I'd appreciate it if you didn't quote me on that.”</blockquote><br/>...bull's-eye, but what a fun and irresistible Texas guy!<br/><br/><b><i>Heaven, Texas</i> is adorable cute</b>, funny and incredibly well written. I think anyone who, like me, loves a c</span>
  <span id="freeText17949397978135078509" style="display:none"><i>Written January 26, 2014</i><br><br><b>5 Huge Stars - stunning romantic and hilarouis fun -<br>I loved every single page - a true joy to read - simply amazing good!!</b><br><br>Our dear hero Bobby Tom Denton:<br><blockquote>“I happen to be immature, undisciplined, and self-centered, pretty much a little boy in a man's body, although I'd appreciate it if you didn't quote me on that.”</blockquote><br>...bull's-eye, but what a fun and irresistible Texas guy!<br><br><b><i>Heaven, Texas</i> is adorable cute</b>, funny and incredibly well written. I think anyone who, like me, loves a charming wallflower heroine and a priceless charmer, but sometimes so narrow-minded, football hero will enjoy, giggle with and remember this story for a long, long time. Sometimes are these old goodies still the very best.. Right?<br><blockquote>
  <a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Cowboys/image_zpsef26872d.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
    <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390764422i/8275102.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpsef26872d.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
  </a>
</blockquote><br>This quite <i>old</i> romance was written nearly twenty years ago, but is this novel still up to scratch? ~ The answer is YES, still in top condition. It was just such a heavenly sweet and charming story with some good nostalgic 1994 feeling in it. Simply a new favorite for this lady.<br><br>~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~*~<br><br>It's all about the wonderful, inexperienced but so resolute <b>Gracie Snow</b> who got a new job as an assistant for a small film company. Her first assignment is to bring the <b>former football star and to be movie star, Bobby Tom Denton,</b> from Chicago to the recording site in his small hometown in Texas. <br><br><b>But Bobby Tom is a <u>stubborn man</u></b>. He is the hero who sometimes have difficulty seeing beyond his halo. Here, try the scantily-clad girl, with a bad permed hair, which in no way matches the women he likes (busty, well-trained, long, slender blondes..) to complicate his life.<br><br><b>But sweet Gracie Snow is a <u>very stubborn woman</u></b> - It will be a match out of the ordinary ~ The American dream guy is challenged by rather unique homely homegrown girl from from Ohio.<br><blockquote>“You're supposed to be my assistant, not a baby-sitter!<br>“One and the same.” <br><br><a href="http://s1332.photobucket.com/user/Li64/media/Cartoon/Couple%20drawings/image_zpsf193521e.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390565402i/8244543.jpg" alt=" photo image_zpsf193521e.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>‘He settled his hat back into position. She was a rookie in her first big game, and he’d never let her see how close she’d come to unseating a champion’ </blockquote><br>There is plenty to say, both about the plot, all the characters and my own feelings, but I'll settle for <b>a few brief comments:</b><br><br># You must <b>have a twinkle in the eye</b> to not get angry at this sometimes so narrow-minded hero. But in the end, you can not resist him .... He is <i>The Charm-Boy</i>! <br># Our heroine is a superb female role model and I wish there were more heroines like her. The absolutely cutest kind.<br># Tom's mother is a widow and her, <b>Suzy's, love-adventure</b> is just as exciting as the main characters. Yummy good!<br># This is a true <i>feel good</i> story or a so-called <b>"rom-com"</b> - read and enjoy!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1390820207i/8283970.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <b>Amusing, smart, well-written, charming, steamy, amazing, memorable</b>, entertaining, romantic, heartwarming, sexy, cute, tender, dramatic, exciting... yes, you probably understand that I loved it.<br><br><b>I LIKE - I still giggles</b><br><br><br>~~~~~~~~~~<br><br><i>I read an fantastic novel <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73086.Kiss_an_Angel" title="Kiss an Angel by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiss an Angel</a> by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/41313.Susan_Elizabeth_Phillips" title="Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Susan Elizabeth Phillips</a> and my good friend Kathleen gave me the excellent advice to pick up <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73084.Heaven__Texas__Chicago_Stars___2_" title="Heaven, Texas (Chicago Stars, #2) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven, Texas</a> next time I needed a sweet and strong <i>Daisy</i> like heroine again. ~ Thank you, Kathleen! You know what I might like. <br><br>...and thanks to her I found this lovely <u>10 year after epilouge</u>. Read it at: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://susanelizabethphillips.com/epilogue-to-heaven-tx/">http://susanelizabethphillips.com/epi...</a> <br>A tempting teaser: </i><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[
  <br>
  <blockquote>‘The children hugged their parents and set off with their grandfather. Bobby Tom watched them go and turned to his wife. “What kind of mother abandons two innocent children to grandparents who are going to stuff them with junk food and keep them up past their bedtime?”<br>“A mother who wants some uninhibited sex with her husband.”</blockquote>
 <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>
  <a data-text-id="17949397978135078509" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_15952182" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/15952182" />
    <a title="Writerlibrarian" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/116025-writerlibrarian"><img alt="Writerlibrarian" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1180996006p2/116025.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/15952182?book_show_action=true">Feb 20, 2008</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Writerlibrarian" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Writerlibrarian" href="/user/show/116025-writerlibrarian">Writerlibrarian</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116025-writerlibrarian?shelf=february-pile">february-pile</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116025-writerlibrarian?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/116025-writerlibrarian?shelf=read2008">read2008</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer15952182" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17189571728764337136">A very average Phillips, with some recycled plot points from other books (or maybe it's the other way around since I haven't read them in order of publishing dates). The good old southern boy character is getting a bit stale. The strip-tease in front of friends the first time the heroine meets the hero is also somewhat icky by now. I really didn't like the lead male character, Bobby Tom, just the name made me just want to run the other way, the character is a boy-men, a very cliché Peter Pan typ</span>
  <span id="freeText17189571728764337136" style="display:none">A very average Phillips, with some recycled plot points from other books (or maybe it's the other way around since I haven't read them in order of publishing dates). The good old southern boy character is getting a bit stale. The strip-tease in front of friends the first time the heroine meets the hero is also somewhat icky by now. I really didn't like the lead male character, Bobby Tom, just the name made me just want to run the other way, the character is a boy-men, a very cliché Peter Pan type of hero. Gracie Snow the lead female character is just... well... paper thin.. not physically, although it's not said, but intellectually, emotionally. The two lead characters kind deserve each other. Why did I keep reading you might ask? Well, because even if her lead characters were very average, Phillips managed to created two very interesting characters in the male's lead mother, Suzy, a 52 years old widow and Waylan Sawyer the town's bad boy, turned philanthropic wealthy man. I wished that the book would have been focused on them. Suzy's still grieving her husband's death after all these years and Waylan has come back and found out he's still very much in love with the girl he couldn't even think of approaching all those years ago. Their story I would have wanted to have more of but it plays second fiddle to the young couples shenanigans. Too bad, there aren't that many well written older woman/man romance out there. </span>
  <a data-text-id="17189571728764337136" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_637059941" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/637059941" />
    <a title="Ⓐlleskelle - teamSøren♗ ⊲I like big b00ks⊳" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18387313-lleskelle---teams-ren-i-like-big-b00ks"><img alt="Ⓐlleskelle - teamSøren♗ ⊲I like big b00ks⊳" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1599759753p2/18387313.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/637059941?book_show_action=true">Jun 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ⓐlleskelle - teamSøren♗ ⊲I like big b00ks⊳" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ⓐlleskelle - teamSøren♗ ⊲I like big b00ks⊳" href="/user/show/18387313-lleskelle---teams-ren-i-like-big-b00ks">Ⓐlleskelle - teamSøren♗ ⊲I like big b00ks⊳</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/18387313-lleskelle---teams-ren-i-like-big-b00ks?shelf=00-on-my-ipad">00-on-my-ipad</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer637059941" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer183504444419063541">⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<b> 3.5 STARS </b>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br/><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456092682r/18189182.jpg?v=1456092686482' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>As <b>SEP</b> recently revealed the cover of her upcoming 8th <b>Chicago Star series</b>’ novel, I was chatting with friends and realized although I enjoyed the series so far, I still hadn’t read book 2 and 6.<br/><br/>I decided then to not leave book 2 unread —<i>or let’s say I felt motivated by threatening OCD friends</i>, and that’s how I’ve found myself spending my Tuesday in the charming company of Bobby Tom Denton, in Heaven Texas.<br/><br/><i>Said no one ever.</i><br/><br/><img src='https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456092713r/18189183.jpg?v=1456092716996' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The man had charming only his name… Strike tha</span>
  <span id="freeText183504444419063541" style="display:none">⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<b> 3.5 STARS </b>⭐️⭐️⭐️⭐️<br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456092682r/18189182.jpg?v=1456092686482" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>As <b>SEP</b> recently revealed the cover of her upcoming 8th <b>Chicago Star series</b>’ novel, I was chatting with friends and realized although I enjoyed the series so far, I still hadn’t read book 2 and 6.<br><br>I decided then to not leave book 2 unread —<i>or let’s say I felt motivated by threatening OCD friends</i>, and that’s how I’ve found myself spending my Tuesday in the charming company of Bobby Tom Denton, in Heaven Texas.<br><br><i>Said no one ever.</i><br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456092713r/18189183.jpg?v=1456092716996" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The man had charming only his name… Strike that. His name was all but charming. <u>I mean, Bobby Tom</u>. I couldn’t read the hero’s name without chuckling. <br><br>But leave it to <b>SEP</b> to make me fall under the charm of an improbable duo. <b>Bobby Tom Denton</b> and <b>Gracie Snow</b> are 2 different people that everything opposed. He’s rich, she’s poor, he’s famous, she’s homely, he’s exuberant, she’s reserved, he’s cocky, she’s no nonsense, he’s overtly sexual… She is a virgin. Yes.<br><br>A 30 years old virgin sent to babysit a cocky retired football player reconverted movie star.<br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456092746r/18189184.jpg?145609274640907" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I liked the idea a lot, I know it does sound cliché, but for what it’s worth, I think if someone could pull this up it definitely was SEP. <br>With promises of banter, teasing, and awkward situations, I let myself wander in Heaven, Texas… And despite Bobby Tom existence, I truly enjoyed myself there. <br><br><b>
  <u>Let it be absolutely clear</u>
</b> : the hero of this story is a chauvinistic asshole doubled as a misogynistic prick! Oh yes.<br><br>The heroine, despite her naivety and out of this world gullibility, was endearing and charming. She was an interesting mix of clueless and feisty woman, and I enjoyed watching her emancipate as the story evolved.<br><br><img src="https://s3.amazonaws.com/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1456092788r/18189185.jpg?v=1456092792372" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Overall a nice story, not sure about the romance part though. For all I could witness, it was mostly one-sided gullible woman’s crush more than an actual relationship with shared feelings. I had troubles coming along with the hero’s douchebaggery, even if he did redeem himself in the end, there were too many occurrences of his conceited male stupidity for me to enjoy the book entirely.<br><br>But <b>Susan Elizabeth Phillips</b> sure does how to tell a story, and despite my qualms regarding the nature of the hero, I enjoyed the verbal joust, cheered for the heroine to get her act on, and even hoped for Bobby Tom’s soul. He could be charming in a way… I guess?<br><br>These books can be read out of order, no problem! And if you aren’t acquainted yet with the absolute reading pleasure that is Susan Elizabeth Phillips, her <b>Chicago Star series</b> is the perfect way to get started!<br><br><i>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer391413167" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer227691918725580959"><br/>AUDIBLE edition. Fantastic. Loved it. Bobby Tom - came across as a bit of a country hick at times but I think that was just his "hometown boy" act!!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561369232i/27717375._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Gracie knew just about as much about American Football as I do!!<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561369329i/27717377._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561369232i/27717376._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/>Great secondary characters ... and an older couple also. Love it. </span>
  <span id="freeText227691918725580959" style="display:none"><br>AUDIBLE edition. Fantastic. Loved it. Bobby Tom - came across as a bit of a country hick at times but I think that was just his "hometown boy" act!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561369232i/27717375._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Gracie knew just about as much about American Football as I do!!<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561369329i/27717377._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1561369232i/27717376._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>Great secondary characters ... and an older couple also. Love it. </span>

<div id="review_1679937492" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1679937492" />
    <a title="Anuradha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/48159983-anuradha"><img alt="Anuradha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590872045p2/48159983.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679937492?book_show_action=true">Jan 13, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Anuradha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Anuradha" href="/user/show/48159983-anuradha">Anuradha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=heroes-who-make-me-throw-up">heroes-who-make-me-throw-up</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=badass-women">badass-women</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=drama-drama-drama">drama-drama-drama</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=ro-ro-romance">ro-ro-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=i-think-it-s-funny">i-think-it-s-funny</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=seeeeeeeex">seeeeeeeex</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=humorists">humorists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/48159983-anuradha?shelf=all-da-feeeeels">all-da-feeeeels</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679937492" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9938910529208351622">Alright you guys, I'm kind of busy right now to read the good stuff, so it's fluff all the way. Well, mostly because reviewing a classic, or some literary fiction requires time for me to do it justice, and it's a lot easier to review fluff. As I've mentioned previously, I read romance for exactly two reasons; a) I've always wanted to find one that I find realistic enough; and b) because ones that fail hard are fun to review. Now, I read some really atrocious romance novels last year, true, but a</span>
  <span id="freeText9938910529208351622" style="display:none">Alright you guys, I'm kind of busy right now to read the good stuff, so it's fluff all the way. Well, mostly because reviewing a classic, or some literary fiction requires time for me to do it justice, and it's a lot easier to review fluff. As I've mentioned previously, I read romance for exactly two reasons; a) I've always wanted to find one that I find realistic enough; and b) because ones that fail hard are fun to review. Now, I read some really atrocious romance novels last year, true, but also some very, very good ones. Like anything by Julie James. Or Sally Thorne's debut, <i>The Hating Game</i>, that knocked my socks off. And then some. As a result, my expectations from fluff were greatly increased, and seeing as how I'd heard so, so much about this series, I went in with high hopes. And how they were dashed, my hopes! How! To an extent, though, this may very well have been a case of "it's not you, it's me". <br /><br />I have been going to Blossom, which is my favourite bookstore in the whole wide world, for about thirteen years now. I go once every few months, whenever I'm home. In these thirteen years, however, never once have I set foot in its rather vast romance section. This time, however, I went with my best friend, who's rather fond of this particular genre. And in the quest of finding <b>
  <i>her</i>
</b> a book that <b>
  <i>I</i>
</b> would actually like, I found, nestled between a raunchy (I'm judging the book by the cover here) historical romance and a Penthouse collection, this book, which of course, I picked because of my aforementioned high hopes. <br /><br />This book wasn't bad, definitely, and had I not been spoilt by some of the good stuff I read last year, I may have ranked this higher. I have to agree that despite her penchant for excruciating descriptions and info dump in some cases, Ms. Phillips is a rather good writer. Very good in fact, were it not for my, er, issues. Gracie Snow is a likable character, sure, and Bobby Tom is not the biggest douchebag. Everything, however, was overdone. It pisses me off when a writer goes out of her (or his, as the case may be) way to highlight a stereotype. Like take Bobby Tom's overt Texan-ness, for instance. If I were to come across a man wearing a stetson and cowboy boots with his bathrobe, I would've laughed until I peed myself or threw up, whichever would've happened first. Gracie, however, found all sorts of wetness and hotness spreading and coursing through her as she saw this...spectacle. And of course, because his "football" player-ness and womanising had to be overdone, he spends all his time with a harem full of large-breasted, curvy, gorgeous women. Blondes, of course. I cringed quite a bit at this. What put me off the most was his "football quiz". That was a prime instance of humour gone bad, way bad. He however did possess a full-sized aortic pump (for the most part), and even though he did douche out at various points, he apologised for it. And meant it. Not that that makes douching around okay, but realising you made a mistake is always the first step.<br /><br />Similarly, with the "homely" and "dowdy" Gracie Snow, her terrible clothes and unattractiveness are emphasised more than it should be. But because her intelligence and strength of character are also equally emphasised, I was able to let that go. Well, mostly. I'm kind of a nit-picker. I also liked that she indulged in sexy lingerie. It gave her character this whole "I'm a vixen underneath it all" attitude, which was very appealing. But because balance had to be restored in the universe, she had to be a virgin. Besides, the whole <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[run away from the cops to save my love life <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> shebang at the end drove me up a fucking wall. Too corny man. Too fucking corny. <br /><br />And now, for the main reason I didn't like the book. Muscles. I don't particularly have a problem with muscles; I do have a problem with extremely muscular men. I prefer the lanky basketball types or the lithe football (I mean, soccer, much as I hate calling it that) types to the built-like-an-ox NFL types. I prefer grace and intelligence over brute strength and general gorilla behaviour. Unfortunately, Bobby Tom belonged to the latter category. I mean, seeing as how this is a series about a football team, this isn't really the book's fault. This is all on me, I agree. But nevertheless, because I'd been gifted with glorious heroes like Cal Morrisey in Jennifer Cruise's <i>Bet Me</i> and any of the drop-dead gorgeous, yet smart, intelligent, empathetic and generous heroes in any of Julie James's romances. I'm sorry, but I have expectations now. And Bobby Tom couldn't hold a candle to any of these men. <br /><br />So yeah, this was a highly disappointing read. I do have expectations from this writer though, so I'm probably going to read another one of her books. Not for a while though. Not for quite a while. </span>
  <a data-text-id="9938910529208351622" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>
