<div id="review_92798370" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/92798370" />
    <a title="Nisha" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2451459-nisha"><img alt="Nisha" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1473558883p2/2451459.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/92798370?book_show_action=true">Mar 06, 2010</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nisha" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nisha" href="/user/show/2451459-nisha">Nisha</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=contemporary-romance">contemporary-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=rake-player-heroes">rake-player-heroes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=sports-romance">sports-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=chick-lit">chick-lit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=marriage-of-convenience-or-arranged">marriage-of-convenience-or-arranged</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=ugly-duckling">ugly-duckling</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=friends-to-lovers">friends-to-lovers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2451459-nisha?shelf=starstruck">starstruck</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer92798370" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer474327565123023352"><b>1st Read: April 25, 2010</b><br/>Bobby Tom is egotistical, selfish, privileged, conceited, and insensitive - not exactly what you look for in a hero. But raised with southern values, he's also charming, sweet, charitable and seems like an overall nice guy, but when fashion disaster, average-looks Gracie Snow enters his life, things get a little screwy for both of them. <br/><br/>Needless to say, I <b>loved</b> it. I loved every part of this gut-wrenching, humorous, yet emotional SM relationship between the H/h. They make</span>
  <span id="freeText474327565123023352" style="display:none"><b>1st Read: April 25, 2010</b><br />Bobby Tom is egotistical, selfish, privileged, conceited, and insensitive - not exactly what you look for in a hero. But raised with southern values, he's also charming, sweet, charitable and seems like an overall nice guy, but when fashion disaster, average-looks Gracie Snow enters his life, things get a little screwy for both of them. <br /><br />Needless to say, I <b>loved</b> it. I loved every part of this gut-wrenching, humorous, yet emotional SM relationship between the H/h. They make a very interesting unlikely couple.<br /><br />Bobby Tom is really a child in a very hot man's body. He has his life on the platter and is actually quite giving - without actually involving himself. He even has a football quiz to find the perfect woman to marry (It's more of an ego rush for him, really). It's just that, B.T. never does what he doesn't like and after being forced into retirement with a knee injury, things don't really go his way. One of those things is Gracie. She's an average looking 30-year-old virgin who has been raised in a Old Age home, that she has never really lived life. She is easy to relate to and is both hilarious and unpredictable, but she has some serious self-esteem issues. It kinda drives their relationship and the climax. B.T. does some really stupid things and thinks some really stupid things. Sometime, I just want to smack the boy/man, but I realized that he can't help it. He's just very slow in the emotional sense. But Gracie, on the other hand, is the absolute opposite. She loves B.T. thinking that there is no way that he could or should love her. <br /><br />As all SEP books, there is a secondary romance for B.T.'s mom with the town villain, Way Sawyer. It's really sweet and painful for both of them - but their love scene is very sensual. They seem to personify a very tragic love story - but they get their HEA. <br /><br />I loved how this book took place in Texas, and they even got to go to Austin (UT Longhorns!) and San Antonio (uh...the Alamo!?!) But most of the time, they were in the small town of Heaven and the set of a movie, kinda. <br /><br />The story was great, both the characters were well fleshed out and were exceedingly entertaining. Then in the end, they finally grew up. SEP is great at writing humor along with the sex, drama and romance, so I just think that she's amazing. <br /><br />*Spoiler alert:<br /><br /><br /><br />My favorite part was the 5 questioned stupid-easy football quiz that Gracie had to pass at the end.<br /><br /><b>2nd Read: April 18, 2012</b><br />Still LOVED it. It's funny how I read this book again, 2 years later. Highly recommend :)<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="474327565123023352" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_441639873" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/441639873" />
    <a title="Kathleen" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen"><img alt="Kathleen" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1365166675p2/13954899.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/441639873?book_show_action=true">Oct 25, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kathleen" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kathleen" href="/user/show/13954899-kathleen">Kathleen</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/13954899-kathleen?shelf=romance-contemp">romance-contemp</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer441639873" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10194337761965511343"><b>NEW epilogue! SEP has posted an <a href='http://susanelizabethphillips.com/epilogue-to-heaven-tx/' rel='nofollow noopener'>epilogue</a> on her website, free. It's set ten years in the future. Sweet! </b><br/><br/>Book 2 of the Chicago Stars series. Romantic, witty, funny, angsty... characterization, humor, passion...and set in a small town called Heaven, Texas.<br/><br/>Quibbles: over-dramatic, and sometimes the setting didn't feel vivid.<br/><br/>The story is sometimes quietly funny, but not in a stupid or slap-stick way. I chuckled numerous times. When I wasn't smiling, I was reading with my jaw on the floor, shocked, w</span>
  <span id="freeText10194337761965511343" style="display:none"><b>NEW epilogue! SEP has posted an <a href="http://susanelizabethphillips.com/epilogue-to-heaven-tx/" rel="nofollow noopener">epilogue</a> on her website, free. It's set ten years in the future. Sweet! </b><br /><br />Book 2 of the Chicago Stars series. Romantic, witty, funny, angsty... characterization, humor, passion...and set in a small town called Heaven, Texas.<br /><br />Quibbles: over-dramatic, and sometimes the setting didn't feel vivid.<br /><br />The story is sometimes quietly funny, but not in a stupid or slap-stick way. I chuckled numerous times. When I wasn't smiling, I was reading with my jaw on the floor, shocked, when Bobby Tom got really mean. I was completely engrossed in the drama. But on a second read, it felt overdone.<br /><br />PLOT: Gracie Snow, almost 30 years old and yet an "old maid" from a small town, becomes football pro Bobby Tom Denton's general factotum, helping him play a role in his first Hollywood film and also organizing a golf tournament for charity in his home town, Heaven (aka Telarosa) Texas. Bobby Tom is trying to figure out what to do with his life, because a bad knee injury has brought an abrupt end to his football career. So he accepts the lead role in a movie. He is bitter and scared, but trying to disguise it behind his legendary charm. Gracie knows him better than he knows himself; she cuts through his BS until he starts to remember the simple pleasures and key values of life. Gracie reminds me a lot of Daisy, in the wonderful circus romance, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73086.Kiss_an_Angel" title="Kiss an Angel by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Kiss an Angel</a>.<br /><br />RELATIONSHIP / ROMANCE: Gracie Snow is an ugly duckling who eventually undergoes a makeover, becoming instantly sassy looking and sexy, but not outstandingly beautiful. She lovingly nurtures the elderly, fights for the underdog, and befriends the lonely. Bobby Tom Denton is full of pride, arrogance, and the kind of ego that comes with a Superbowl ring. However, gradually SEP reveals his underlying heart of gold. He eventually falls head over heels for Gracie, but it takes a while for him to realize this, because she is not a sex bomb, not a "Grade A prime cut" as he chauvinistically thinks. Her warm heart, honesty, and strong, stubborn personality win him over, slowly. Along the way, the sexual tension slowly builds, with lots of laughs and a few serious scenes along the way. <br /><br />It ends with a grovel scene. The best grovel scene ever, because Bobby Tom has completely fumbled the ball.<br /><br />WEAK SPOTS: Drama, the drama! Why does Gracie need to be a virgin? At her age? Also, it ends abruptly. I wanted an epilogue after the grovel scene. Nope. But. Wait! <b>NEW epilogue! SEP has posted an <a href="http://susanelizabethphillips.com/epilogue-to-heaven-tx/" rel="nofollow noopener">epilogue</a> on her website, free. It's set ten years in the future. Sweet! </b><br /><br />I also recommend book 3 in the series. I loved the blend of humor, wit, romance, and angst. In <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73080.Nobody_s_Baby_But_Mine__Chicago_Stars___3_" title="Nobody's Baby But Mine (Chicago Stars, #3) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Nobody's Baby But Mine</a>, we briefly go back to Heaven, Texas.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10194337761965511343" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer624585938" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2456425730283448136"><b>Rate: 5 solid stars</b><br/><br/><i>“I know how you felt about each other, Mom. I saw it every day. Maybe that's why I've never had much interest in getting married myself. Because I've always wanted the same thing.”<br/><br/>Gracie danced past in his peripheral vision, and at that exact moment, the fact that he could have the same thing his parents had had all those years hit him so hard he nearly stumbled.Jesus. As he held his mother in his arms and felt his father's presence, he knew that same intimacy was right here w</i></span>
  <span id="freeText2456425730283448136" style="display:none"><b>Rate: 5 solid stars</b><br /><br /><i>“I know how you felt about each other, Mom. I saw it every day. Maybe that's why I've never had much interest in getting married myself. Because I've always wanted the same thing.”<br /><br />Gracie danced past in his peripheral vision, and at that exact moment, the fact that he could have the same thing his parents had had all those years hit him so hard he nearly stumbled.Jesus. As he held his mother in his arms and felt his father's presence, he knew that same intimacy was right here waiting for him on the other side of the dance floor. He loved her. The knowledge almost knocked him to his knees. He loved his Gracie Snow—funny clothes, bossy manner, and all. She was his entertainment, his conscience, the mirror into his soul. She was his resting place. Why hadn't he understood this weeks ago?</i><br /><br />Oh man. Another winner from SEP. I LOVED Gracie and Bobby Tom's story. She, the down-to-earth plain miss and he, the superbowl superhero. Even better the secondary story between Suzy and Way was the little cherry on top of the cake and added just that much more depth to the plot. This book was the perfect concoction of wit and emotion, and I even found myself tearing up at towards the end!<br /><br />For those of you who haven't read Susan Elizabeth Phillips enjoy chick lit or contemporary romance I would definitely recommend you pick up one of these books by her:<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73089.Match_Me_If_You_Can__Chicago_Stars___6_" title="Match Me If You Can (Chicago Stars, #6) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Match Me If You Can</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/373606.Ain_t_She_Sweet" title="Ain't She Sweet by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Ain't She Sweet</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73095.Dream_a_Little_Dream__Chicago_Stars___4_" title="Dream a Little Dream (Chicago Stars, #4) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Dream a Little Dream</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73064.Natural_Born_Charmer__Chicago_Stars___7_" title="Natural Born Charmer (Chicago Stars, #7) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Natural Born Charmer</a><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/8437379.Call_Me_Irresistible__Wynette__Texas__6_" title="Call Me Irresistible (Wynette, Texas #6) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Call Me Irresistible</a><br />and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73084.Heaven__Texas__Chicago_Stars___2_" title="Heaven, Texas (Chicago Stars, #2) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven, Texas</a><br />(I just thought I might share some of my SEP faves with you)</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer3002710560224921146">My first exposure to SEP was <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73084.Heaven__Texas__Chicago_Stars___2_' title='Heaven, Texas (Chicago Stars, #2) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips' rel='nofollow noopener'>Heaven, Texas</a> and, therefore, it has a special place in my heart. This is not just another bad-boy football superstar with a diabolic gleam meets 30 year-old wallflower story. These characters had depth. <a class='jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction'>(view spoiler)</a><span class='spoilerContainer' style='display: none'>[I actually had to call my best friend - who doesn't read romance books, but loves football - and tell her about the scene where Gracie discovers Bobby Tom reviewing the video of his career-ending injury over and over again.   <span id="freeText3002710560224921146" style="display:none">My first exposure to SEP was <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73084.Heaven__Texas__Chicago_Stars___2_" title="Heaven, Texas (Chicago Stars, #2) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">Heaven, Texas</a> and, therefore, it has a special place in my heart. This is not just another bad-boy football superstar with a diabolic gleam meets 30 year-old wallflower story. These characters had depth. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[I actually had to call my best friend - who doesn't read romance books, but loves football - and tell her about the scene where Gracie discovers Bobby Tom reviewing the video of his career-ending injury over and over again. I fell in love with him before that, but that just made me sob. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br /><br />Loved the road trip, Bobby Tom's menopausal mother and her secondary romance, the actress he works with on the movie, Gracie’s make-over followed by him wondering who the hell’s driving his convertible, the ice cream scene, Gracie's ideas for his old house, how you could see them falling in love as the pages turned, their real-sounding fights, LOL moments, and…well, everything. This one went directly onto my ‘re-read for comfort' bookshelf and sent me to the bookstore to pick up more of the Chicago Stars series.<br /><br />Oh, and the end of Heaven, Texas is absolutely, positively worth waiting for. Actually, it is one of the best endings in many a romance book. Don’t click the following spoiler if you haven’t already read the book. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[SEP has an ability to make me laugh and cry at the same time, and she perfected it in Heaven, Texas. At the end, Gracie is down on the rough ground with Bobby Tom. They’re on the side of the road after he’s broken out of jail to chase after her, everybody follows along and she’s protecting him so it's really a comedy of errors-tear jerker. Question: If that happens, does it count as a groveling scene?<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer98498535" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1270459712045229251"><a href='http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2014/04/review-heaven-texas-by-susan-elizabeth-phillips.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333934i/693541.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Gracie Snow is a completely innocent, stubborn, but curious 30 year old seeking adventure. Luckily her new job working for a Hollywood studio should provide all the excitement she hopes for. Her first assignment is to collect Bobby Tom Denton, a former American football player, and bring him to the film set so they can start filming his first film. Simple? Not really, but Gracie risks life, limb and her heart to get him there. <br/><br/>I love this book, it always comes to mind when I need something s</span>
  <span id="freeText1270459712045229251" style="display:none"><a href="http://www.underthecoversbookblog.com/2014/04/review-heaven-texas-by-susan-elizabeth-phillips.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380333934i/693541.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Gracie Snow is a completely innocent, stubborn, but curious 30 year old seeking adventure. Luckily her new job working for a Hollywood studio should provide all the excitement she hopes for. Her first assignment is to collect Bobby Tom Denton, a former American football player, and bring him to the film set so they can start filming his first film. Simple? Not really, but Gracie risks life, limb and her heart to get him there. <br><br>I love this book, it always comes to mind when I need something sweet and funny to relax with. It is particularly effective when used in tangent with a glass of wine and a bubble bath! The charming characters, romance and humour never let me down. <br><br>What always has me coming back for more is the main characters; Gracie Snow and Bobby Tom Denton. You could feel Bobby Tom's charisma and personality pouring out of the book and reeling you in, not that he was perfect, he has an ego a mile wide, but you love him anyways. And Gracie was so funny and sweet; I couldn't help but like her. Some of the situations that Gracie finds herself in are hilarious, I couldn't wait to see what she would do next. <br><br>This book also has secondary romance between an older couple, which was a nice addition, it didn't get lots of page time but it was still an enjoyable part of the book. <br><br>If you haven't tried this book, I highly recommend you pick it up, it is perfect for either snuggling up to in the winter and tanning with in the summer! </span>
  <a data-text-id="1270459712045229251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

  <span id="freeText3839164975778238808" style="display:none">The list of reasons I love this book is a mile long; great writing, well developed hilarious characters, strong heroine, hero that may appear to be a manwhore, but is actually a really good guy, fake relationship trope, small town setting, sports romance, etc. I could continue listing another million reasons. But the most important is just how the book made me feel happy. I was happy reading every bit of it. Nothing was too over the top, nothing annoyed me. <br /><br />I’m obviously over 20 years late to the Susan Elizabeth Phillips party, but better late than never. The story was still very relevant, there just weren’t any references to Facebook or twitter and that was a relief.<br /><br />Highly recommend this book. </span>

<div id="review_68415240" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/68415240" />
    <a title="Juliana Philippa" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1378820-juliana-philippa"><img alt="Juliana Philippa" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1597182219p2/1378820.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/68415240?book_show_action=true">Aug 21, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Juliana Philippa" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Juliana Philippa" href="/user/show/1378820-juliana-philippa">Juliana Philippa</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-read-multiple-times">0-read-multiple-times</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-own-in-dead-tree-form">0-own-in-dead-tree-form</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-reviewed">0-reviewed</a>,

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=0-own-in-dead-tree-form-mass-market">0-own-in-dead-tree-form-mass-market</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=4-half-to-5-romance-contemporary">4-half-to-5-romance-contemporary</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=4-half-to-5-romance-books">4-half-to-5-romance-books</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=cr-heroine-plain-jane">cr-heroine-plain-jane</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1378820-juliana-philippa?shelf=cr-heroine-not-confident">cr-heroine-not-confident</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer68415240" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12496744388897782724"><i>Heaven, Texas</i> was absolutely wonderful! It's my first book by Phillips and although I got it from the library, I'm definitely putting it on my "To Buy" list, since I know I will want to reread this book several times. So cute and very funny; the interactions between the hero and heroine were priceless and the supporting characters were interesting and added to the story.<br/><br/>When I was preparing to venture into contemporary romance and did "research" (lol) on Rachel Gibson's books, <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60223.See_Jane_Score__Chinooks_Hockey_Team___2_' title='See Jane Score (Chinooks Hockey Team, #2) by Rachel Gibson' rel='nofollow noopener'>See Jane Score</a> see</span>
  <span id="freeText12496744388897782724" style="display:none"><i>Heaven, Texas</i> was absolutely wonderful! It's my first book by Phillips and although I got it from the library, I'm definitely putting it on my "To Buy" list, since I know I will want to reread this book several times. So cute and very funny; the interactions between the hero and heroine were priceless and the supporting characters were interesting and added to the story.<br /><br />When I was preparing to venture into contemporary romance and did "research" (lol) on Rachel Gibson's books, <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/60223.See_Jane_Score__Chinooks_Hockey_Team___2_" title="See Jane Score (Chinooks Hockey Team, #2) by Rachel Gibson" rel="nofollow noopener">See Jane Score</a> seemed to be the hit/masterpiece that everyone raved over (and understandably!!). Likewise, <i>Heaven, Texas</i> was pretty universally lauded in the reviews I read on Amazon, so I thought it would be a good one to start with—and I was not mistaken: completely fabulous! Plus, it definitely tapped into the little spot I have in my heart for Texas after living in San Antonio for a few years when I was younger. Great romance; definitely recommend.<br /><br />Gracie was a wonderful heroine and I loved that there was no game-playing on her part; she was always so honest, thoughtful, forthright, sweet, but also intelligent, bold, stubborn, sassy, and when she commits herself to something ... get out of her way, because she's determined! People were always wanting a part of Bobby Tom (the hero) or wanting some favor/monetary gift from him, and I really liked that Phillips made it such a pointed and emphasized aspect of Gracie's character that she wasn't like that and consciously wanted to be different from all of them—wanted to be the one who finally just <i>gave</i> to him (her friendship, love, affection, etc.), instead of <i>taking</i> from him.<br /><br />It took me awhile to get used to Bobby Tom's name, but after about the first chapter it seemed perfect for him. His character was utterly enjoyable—Phillips writes him as SO much more than just a football-player-jock; he's intelligent, witty, amusing, really very giving and kind, and of course 110% charming. Gracie is able to see past the charming-always-grinning persona that he presents so often and pretty much right off the bat, she knows he's much smarter and complicated than most people give him credit for—or than he wants people to realize.</span>
  <a data-text-id="12496744388897782724" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1785369150" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1785369150" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1785369150?book_show_action=true">Oct 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=steamy">steamy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1785369150" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3637959512256715537">Well that was a disappointment. I kinda liked Bobby Tom in the first book, though we don't actually see him much. It turns out, he doesn't improve with acquaintance. He's arrogant and entitled and stubborn and immature. Yeah, there's some charm and a sense of honor buried under there somewhere, but those aspects get overwhelmed by his innate selfishness too often to actually count.<br/><br/>I really liked Gracie, though, and that let me plow through his stupidity. SEP excels at the interactions between he</span>
  <span id="freeText3637959512256715537" style="display:none">Well that was a disappointment. I kinda liked Bobby Tom in the first book, though we don't actually see him much. It turns out, he doesn't improve with acquaintance. He's arrogant and entitled and stubborn and immature. Yeah, there's some charm and a sense of honor buried under there somewhere, but those aspects get overwhelmed by his innate selfishness too often to actually count.<br /><br />I really liked Gracie, though, and that let me plow through his stupidity. SEP excels at the interactions between her characters and that does a lot to ameliorate the worst aspects of a leading man I don't care for. You could see from the start that she'd be the making of him and that she'd do it with kindness and an unfeigned love that gave rather than took—something completely unfamiliar with Bobby Tom as pretty much all his other relationships are the opposite (all about what he can do for others). And I particularly liked her interactions with the other women around BT.<br /><br />The secondary characters weren't as strong in this one as in others. I <em>did</em> like BT's co-star (Michelle? Nicole?) and her solid marriage. A woman he had to make out and simulate sex with and yet who was completely devoted to her marriage and baby. Her friendship with Gracie was a highlight and fun contrast with the designing women otherwise cluttering up the place. Less fun was the secondary romance with BT's mom. It started creepy and I never really got over that.<br /><br />Anyway, I liked the book well-enough, but only three-stars worth. The ending had BT do too much damage on his way to growing up and I hated the continued hits on Gracie. Way to mess up the grand gesture, BT...<br /><br /><strong>A note about the series</strong>: You really can read this one independently of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/73070.It_Had_to_Be_You__Chicago_Stars___1_" title="It Had to Be You (Chicago Stars, #1) by Susan Elizabeth Phillips" rel="nofollow noopener">It Had to Be You</a>, but I don't know why you'd want to. It's a better book and way more fun.<br /><br /><strong>A note about Steamy</strong>: There are a couple explicit sex scenes, but an extra for BT's mom and a lot of added foreplay as well. Still the middle of my steam tolerance, but edging toward the high side. I really liked BT's care for Gracie's initial virgin status, but that's offset entirely by the creepy bit we see with his mom's new "beau".</span>
  <a data-text-id="3637959512256715537" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uJqwuLGCT3eSIS9Lo9pJTNq8soAfqmYpjpC6i6qyMA3TE6MwDMujms3ceul703JhvYAcJhmHjp6n5AZtFF0w8Q==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('uUqyCPEpuWNtsyMtnMxjNPLwsr87IztpWV5zDAxMMDDSw6GATGBVjjJOdo9ExVgZlcwcGT0O095wKs/qsqMwzA==')})
  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer17266343882498779525">SUSAN ELIZABETH PHILLIPS<br/><br/>Susan Elizabeth Phillips is the creator of the sports romance, beginning with her 1989 bestseller, FANCY PANTS. An internationally acclaimed author, her books have been published in over 30 languages. She’s the only four-time recipient of the Romance Writers of America’s prestigious Favorite Book of the Year Award, and a recipient of their Lifetime Achievement Award. <br/><br/>Susan'</span>
  <span id="freeText17266343882498779525" style="display:none">SUSAN ELIZABETH PHILLIPS<br /><br />Susan Elizabeth Phillips is the creator of the sports romance, beginning with her 1989 bestseller, FANCY PANTS. An internationally acclaimed author, her books have been published in over 30 languages. She’s the only four-time recipient of the Romance Writers of America’s prestigious Favorite Book of the Year Award, and a recipient of their Lifetime Achievement Award. <br /><br />Susan's newest book, DANCE AWAY WITH ME, was published in hardcover, ebook and audiobook in June 2020. She is also the highly acclaimed author of both the CHICAGO STARS football series and the Wynette, Texas books. <br /><br />In addition to being a New York Times, Publisher’s Weekly, and USA Today bestseller, she is a hiker, lazy gardener, horrible singer, passable cook, passionate reader, wife, mother of two grown sons, and grandmother. <br /><br />You can visit Susan on Facebook, Twitter, Instagram or on her website.<br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.facebook.com/SusanElizabethPhillipsNovels">https://www.facebook.com/SusanElizabe...</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twitter.com/sepauthor">https://twitter.com/sepauthor</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/SEPauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/SEPauthor/</a><br /><br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://susanelizabethphillips.com/">http://susanelizabethphillips.com/</a><br /><br /></span>
